arge fourescore numbre sothly tale pand thelemus myghty euryale two manly men armes sage dyomede came voyage pand polyphebus brought shippes seuen phyneus hardy kynge enleuen pand prothoylus specifye brought fyfty shyppes vnto nauye fro demenesa myghtye regyon pand carpenor made mencion brought fyfty eke capadye coutrey great prouynce whiche king ptricorius beysa lorde kynge brought two twenty eke comyng fynally shall lye full many shyppe nauye mo guydo maketh rehersayle towarde troye grekes sayle homer discrypcion grekes shyppes maketh mencion shortly affyrmyng ye man neuer borne nombre shippes sawe toforne countyng shyppes palamydes brought nombre encrease whan lordes aforsayd euerychone kynges duke erles one assembled without wene afore hauen called athene famous kynge great agamenowne wyse worthy hye renown prynce gouernour grekes hooste anone dyd labour busy cure waker dylygence hyghe aduyse inwarde prouydence deliberate wisely nede procede matter castyng vp downe reuoluynge hygh discreciowne may begyn ende conclude well wylfulnesse ne shende hooly purpose rakelnesse ne none haste without auysenesse may afore wysely see fynally felicitye accomplyshe may purpose certayne pand king vpon large playne citie lyttle stronde lordes wyll nothyng wonde haue counsaile wyse agamenon makyng anone conuocacyon suche great inspeciall syttyng fyrste see royall lordes eueryche see lyke hye lowe degree tumulte stynted scylence ye prese gyne hym audyence whan anone full sobre wyse began tale shall deuyse syres quod praye taketh hede noble renowmede wysedome worthinesse manhode eke hyghe prowesse knyghthode reporte fame thrughout ye world reboudeth name doubtlesse floure chyualrye men may fynde companye sawe euer manly men yfeare together met younge freshe couragyous also well besene haue lykely syth worlde began without raskayle many knyghtly man kynges duke many lorde wyll one accorde one herte assembled place yf fortune goddes grace behynde iourney repreue may fayle purpose achyeue deme hym playnly arage worse wood durste voyage wyse perturbe presume take agayne v outher assume myght hym malys exscyte worthynesse neuer solyte v prouoke ire offence ne shulde mortall recompence aquyte mede lyeth myght assemble many worthy knyght amouges whiche hundred yet mo coulde chese able go manly force knyghtly suffysaunce take hym vengeaunce vpon troyans hym selfe alone whyche gathred echone men suffycient execute summe entent accomblyshe felicitee cause meane whiche assembled ben together hye lowe pand also vnknowe howe shamefully troyans haue v greued prouoked v wylfully ymeued ryse agayne haue recure right wronges done force myght wherfore let v one assent wyll sette haue ryght skyll redresse fynde nowe complaine one harte busy peyne vpon troyans werre make suppose shall awake shall lerne thense wende remembre worldes ende hereafter shall dare take hande presume grece lande bolde haue lyfe space agayne grekes trespace whose offence sayth late within herte deadly brennyng hate feruent hete gredy yre fro day day setteth v fyre reneweth constreynt peine inwardely yf shall fayne must reason hygh greuaunce selfe enforce vengeaunce ryght requereth iuste sorowe compelleth v eue morowe troyans harmes bewreke stoppe tounges speake reprefe villanye must attones shapen remedye foen henseforth may haue drede worse v god forbed tyme commynge yf pacience lykely suffer importable offence passe forth take hede syth neuer yet grekes coulde reade man dyd reprefe name iustly might rebounde shame withouten quyte agayne thrugh manhode openly playne man myght seyne ere wyse reporte amysse pne shall dyssymule case chere oppressed dredfull face let slyde lyghtly ouer go great offence late ydo might happly tourne v oures great reprefe successours tune comming shamfully bespoke grekes durste worke vpon foon whiche may ensure sythe one wyll refourme wronge therwithall mighty stronge coulde brede length ryght reherse power strength durste euer worthynesse assayle ne shulde withouten fayle repente herte ende rewe saue troyans daye newe wylfulnesse foly rage lande made voyage vnware v pray home wente whiche shall full hastely repente trespace great offencyowne pfor worlde knoweth vp downe late gone grekes fewe vpon troyans power dyd shewe slewe kyng called lamedowne father pryam kyng towne cleane fordyd toures citye slewe vp commynaltye grekes sworde yt list spare amonges v seruitude care compleine harme yt may recured may stande full assured agayne v holde chaumpartye haue worthy companye lykely thousande acheue foure fyue lyghtly myght preue yet one thynge affyrme well dare cummyng troyans well ware labour diligence agaynst v maken resystence al myght knowe doute gather frendes countreys helpe strength nede v withstande may spede pbut fynally one thynge counsayle hauen ferther sayle may fortunate one assent make ambassyat prudently wende delos haste sende whiche yle little besyde discretely iourney prouyde may haue better hap grace apollo patron place haue maye speade fynall answere great nede exployet shall fall ye wyll assenten counsayle eke leste pand echone thought best condescende conclusyon without contradiction attones without drede preyse counseyle wise rede therupon distretly ought sayth story euen thus wroughte phow achilles patroclus sent delos receiue answere god apollo shuld spede ayenst ye troyans cap xvii tyme agamenon concluded fully reason ye haue herde sentence fyned grekes herte full enclyned one voyce accorded plainly thus achilles also patroclus comon profyt syth sage shall take ye charge message appollo answere gone shyppe haste anone sayle forth large sea towarde delos prosperitee aryued ycome lande whiche yle vnderstande myne auctor sayth without le hath scyte amonges cyclades men rockes haue muche amyd see called helespontico whyche yle make descrypcion must awhyle make disgressyon fro matter myne auctour doth yle isodorus soth reherseth playnly latona quene appollo fyrst dyane shene ychilded hath iubyter lorde whan iuno suche discorde wryte ouyde lyttell whyle befell lyttell yle temple whylom dedicate vnto appollo also consecrate worshyp phetonysses deuyne meane woman deuyneresses dead men false sorceress one whylom reysed samuel loue saule byble tell temple large longe olde statue pured golde full great hyghe huge weyght therin deuocion voyde reason hasty wood without dreade also toty theyr heade voyde power myght haue foote stande vpryght yet iargaunt pye right pale cheared glasye eye full reason til winde spent woman vynolent veryly beast vnreasonable dome holde theim eke vnable accepted companye whan theyr tunge wadeth lye ne may bryng forth worde pand thus bachus strog mighty lord ful oft causeth folkes erre debate maken werre hastynesse nede wherfore wysedome men drede sleyghty workyng fall snare feble braines measure spare vnwarely arested take bachus make theim shake feuer worse tercyen custome cotydyen alterat bachus myghty iou affered tourning hous fordreynt drye lande hath lost vse foote hande strawe playeth lyke ape deuoutly ginneth gape noddeth oft wyth iowsy heade heauy cappe leade condicion entre maye relegyon myghty bachus habylite whych lorde hath souereynte hony mylke therto bawme ryche also lordshyp hath high power diuine grape euery vyne theim nouryshe influence honour attayne tree delycious paradyse precious nouther sight semelinesse egall fayrnesse pryde surquidrye whan sayde god syt hye wyll lyke also set see high north passyng degre cast downe wyth legyons fayre heauenly mansyons sodaynly pyt hel perpetually dwell sayde whan fel ferre fell thou thou morowe sterre middes stone bryght persyng fyery theyr lyght whilom thy great bryghtnesse called lucifer christ sayeth expresse gospell sawe fro heauen sathan descende lyke fyery leuene olde serpent lowe yfall hebrues theyr tunge call pbemoth doth latin playne expresse beast rude full cursednesse vile serpent grace whych sea large great space wyth foule adder hath mansyon vnto mankynde illusyon whylom sawe holy monke brada sayled forthe occyan thorowen deiect pyt horryble foule hydous credible abide tortuous serpent vnto daye playnly iudgement malyce enuyed mankynde whych ginnes sleightes find came father first paradyse deceyue bet deuyse couertly worme passage toke serpent lyknesse ymage cheare loke countenaunce lyke mayde hath resemblaunce woman recordeth bede deceytes rather spede meane face onely elles behynde clerkes telles lyke serpent wombe backe tayle whan gan assaile towarde eue whan gan glyde fyrst enquereth toke asyde god forbad theim eten tree whych eate sothly shulden like goddes knowing good yll right forthwith gan fulfyll fendes hest theyr eyen vnclosed theyr gylt sodaynly deposed paradyse wretchednesse lyue labour sorowe distresse thus fende whan fyrst toke fourme snake woman loke made tunge heade meue false engene mankinde greue doth theim trauayled wycked spyrytes vexed assayled meue theyr tunges falsly breake blasphemy thinge yt speake serpent leuiathan continuing aye falsely gan cursed idolles dombe deafe blinde ful oft speaketh spyrytes finde fendes dauid idolatrye cause ought espye sawe matter knowe ilyche well high lowe perauenture pleasaunce hath grounde put remembraunce false goddes mawmentrye theim poesye ye storye resorteth soone agayne achilles ye haue herd saine patroclus haue waye ynome temple thyther ycome haue aunswere theyr embassadrye great apollo whych may lye ye pryestes haue theyr counsaile take temple praie wake tyll may finde vnto theyr entente haue aunswere time conuenient theyr purpose leysure oportune pand one herte longe contune praying fastyng oblacions wyth sacrifise sundrye orysons tofore god awayting alwaye fast tyll theim answered last softe voyce sayde achilles twye home grekes fast thou hye thou hyther sente saye sothly sume entent shalbe fulfylled withouten wordes mo shall troye go abyde many stronge battayle last withouten fayle ten yeares daye win shall towne brynge playnly destructiowne wall toures fall shal ruyne al theyr purpose fyne kyng priamus hecuba wife theyr sone mortall stryfe shall slayne brother brother fine may none shal none escape place grekes liketh vnto grace routhe mercy take thus ende make aunswere achilles glad light hert al myght thanketh apollo blesfull eure sodeynly sorte aduenture selfe tyme befell wonder thynge troye pryamus kynge sent bysshop case haue answere named calchas came fool without prese houre whyle achilles present man great scyence meane calchas experyence especially calculacion sorte also dyuinacion lerned astronomye whan tyme dyd espye haue answere conuenient appollo lyke entent heretofore maked memorye entred oratorye doyng rytes obseruaunces lyke custome circumstaunces besely gan knele praye thinges deuoutly saye god crye call ful stronge apollo would tho prolonge sodaynly aunswere gan attame sayd calchas twies name right wel ware thou ne tourne agayne troye towne vayne finally lerne thinge shorte tyme shall destroyed sothe whych may denyed wherfore wil thou alyed grekes achilles go theim anone shall haue haue disclosed victorye honour may disposed fatall ne may varye thou theim shalt necessarye counseling yeuing rede right helping good spede worde rose vp calchas achilles went easy pace whan came presence great honour muche reuerence receiued like estate soone confederate swore togyther bonde assuraunce al one withouten varyaunce haste togyther gone theyr shippes shope theym forth anone patroclus goyng theyr syde hale vp anker longer byde sayle forthe calchas twayne toward grece theim nedeth complaine winde wawe till aryued athene stode vpon sea large citye olde foundacion achilles kyng agamenon hath calchas brought also patroclus whan grekes storye telleth v assembled together went tofore king calchas represent lordes longer dwell right anone achilles gan tell without abode delos mette tofore apollo aunswer fette god hath playnly determyned grekes purpose shal fyned vpon troians bad calchas also wyse troye go grekes abyde styll tyll theyr purpose fynally fulfyll whiche thyng grekes glad chere calchas accepte herte full entere one confederate bonde one water londe without chaunge varyaunce othe made put remembraunce agayne fully hym assure cheryshe hym whyle theyr lyfe may dure weale wo made ende parte lodgyng wende till morne sterry nyght aurora gladded wt light phebus beames grekes vp aryse goddes many sacryfyce honour may deuoutly holdyng feast daye rytes meynt loue drede remembraunce good spede answere ye goddes haue sent agreable vnto entent patroclus achilles amonges prese calchas come tofore agamenon lordes syttynge enuyron lyke estate eche place dewe humbly gan salewe vpon knee sobre countenaunce prayed displesaunce stynte whyle gyue hym audyence ryght anone made sylence amonge calchas gan abrayde euen thus full sobrely sayd oh syres quod lordes dere kynges prince duke noble echone worthy famous eke manly vertuous whiche place present fyne chiefe entent cause also ye echone assembled troye gone power great strength purpose longe drawe length differred forth day daye damage platly naye longe ye soiourne yle trowe ye pryam whyle hath espyes amonge pryuely wote wele saye faythfully knowe fyne gouernaunce whyles may make purueaunce hym defende ye ydell reste semeth sothly ye beste abydyng suche delayes great harme may fal certayne nay preue thus playnly whyle yee enmyes graunte lybertee puruey may mighty hand enforce power withstande fryendes allyaunce leysour make ordinaunce foly ye dyfferre syth ye ready make werre ennemyes euery circustraunce nothyng may quarell auaunce hasty suite sharper byte iron hoote tyme smyte abyde tyll colde wyl neither plye folde go sette vpon one accorde shyppe anone within borde enhaste tyme remewe might quarell pursue agaynst haue trespassed many dayes somer passed many monthes ronne ouerslyde titan oft chare hath ryde east west wawes depe streames bathed whyles ye slepe spent tyme place thus whyle wynde called zephirus beningly enspyred hath alofte attempre aier wether fayre soft calme sea wawes styll playne whyles ye waste dayes vayne foon therto taken hede wil suppose drede bolde set lite truste forsothe wyll quite trewlye like bounde thynke ye haue goddes founde toward bening fortunate honour saued high lowe estate shall forthe ingratytude prouoke theim purpose delude wylfully slouthe good fortune wonder though contune towardes shewe theyr grace wherfore reade hense pace shapeth longer lye whyle wether fayre clere lusty somer abydeth hete wynter come wyth raynes wete season freshe grene speake herte platly mene exployt alder ease angre please forth haste ye shyppe wende tale ende phowe grekes nauye retourning athene distressed tempest toke castel ye troians called saranaba ca xviii one codesceded aduyse haue wel comeded al haste agamenon grete lusty time season swete hastyng grekes high lowe made soude trumpe shipward blowe echone bidding obey theyr shippes go right weye without abode longer dwell shuld nomber tell theyr shippes syth ye haue herde afore nedeth reherse se might auayle forthe dresse bega sayle sothe playnly wene great nauye neuer yet ysene worlde together met winde good yt let theyr waye fyrst whan begon soone gan shene son clearnesse chaunge bryght face dimme cloudes gan light enbrace sodaynly full ougly wise heauen dercke wynde gan ryse hydous thunder leuene clere smote mast bryght fyere blacknes smoky reyne blindeth eyre nothyng may sene wawes gan ryse alofte theyr shippes fell nothyng softe plonge downe theyr toppes smyte theim thought wanted lyte haue dead selfe stounde tyll calchas hath craft yfounde cause orysons charmes incantacions made sodaynly tempest appease wt craft done theim right great ease founde cause euerydele dyane lyked nothyng wele grekes dursten take hande bolde parte stronde sea maner wyse maner sacrifyce nouther offer tofore gothe thyng goddesse wroth towarde grekes saylynge sea echone wende haue drowned tyll laste kyng agamenon hath counsayle information wyse calchas made sette vp londe yle faste shyppes bonde aulydes little yle hyghte whiche fonde vnware syghte lyttle temple oratorye founded olde made memory great dyane anone wente full deuoutly offerynge present quemed oblacions lay longe orison rytes vsed lawe tell sawe tempest gan adawe bokes maken mencion touchyng thyng agamenon ouyde lyst rehersen boke kyng owne doughter toke effygenya benynge face chere endelonge vpon aultere mayde layde dispoyled wede tofore dyane maken blede fyne heauenly quene bloud innocent clene appease myght quemen rage goddesse gracious visage hath mercy meynt magnifycence suffer mayde full innocence gyltlesse temple slawe hath myracle away body drawe conserued anoy smerte stede vnwarely caste herte deth bokes maken mynde agamenon fyrst gan grace fynde goddes modefye cruell ire cleren gan skye sea waxe calme wether fayre phebus eke glade eyre gan shewe newe beames caste sea kynge faste vnto shyppe repayred agayne thrugh helpe clerk saine lady quene wayes passage goddesse called voyage sentence opynyon worke calculacion gyn dome astronomy magnifye tenth twelfe house saye moste gracious best fortuned clere shade haue comeforte aspectes glade planettes standynge tho good state meane suche planettes fortunate voyage iourney make tyme agamenon hath take happy waye shypped good houre taken hath sea grekes wether agreable eolus hath maked acceptable wynde eyre hoole wyll nouther loude playnely styll meane mery made blowe attayne lyttell throwe certayne boundes troye citie vnto castell stode vpon sea right wonder strong though lite name whiche thoughe dare liste wryte meane dare called frygius yet auctours reherse sothly thus saranaba ycalled rounde aboute diched well walled hyghe toures rounde square wide vnder went sea fast besyde hauen able ryuayle whiche playnely grekes wyl fayle power myghtely aryue maugre tho agayne stryue might well denied except espyed alone castell dwell whiche anone herde tell commynge proudely berde mete nothyng aferde issue downe vnto stronde purpose onely lette londe might wolde auayle grekes proudely assayle ne myght defence endure wende haue assure demyng grekes plainly sea weryed faynted haue longe saylinge parbraked forbroke wherfore cast haue wroke sodeinly sette head put selfe aduenture drede rakelnesse vnaduysedly wherof selfe vnhappely befell grekes mette speres longe swerdes sharpe whet eche manhode shewe cause troyans fewe yssue dyd folyfye fyelde parted egally grekes innumerable mete troyans able tyme mighten suffyse toke passyng hygh empryse yet wold nothing wtdrawe tyll wounded yslawe ouerlayne grekes vtterly bore downe cruelly mercylesse guydo doth reporte behoueth home agayne resorte verye nede necessytee attones gan flee meane suche lefte alyue castell hasted full blyue ne myght longer holde fyelde agaynst grekes spere shielde feble shortely conclude abyde great multitude flee grekes great pace ne cease sewe chase full hastyly castell gate entre cruell fate kyll slea hye lowe spare none ne lyst wyght knowe none estate felly oppresse fonde golde eke rychesse vnto shyppe caryed anone castell ne lefte stone aboue tourned vp downe wall toure chiefe dongeowne nothynge stode vnder myne whan brought vnto ruyne grekes anone shyppes haste one assent purposen faste without abode one wyll herte fro hauen playnly dyuerte sayle towarde tenedowne stronge castell whyche troye towne distaunce thense syxe myle stode ful treasour rychesse good replenyshed habundaunce theyr ordynaunce ysayled haue theyr iourney safe sound fro sea taken haue grounde theyr plesaunce wonder agreable syght place delectable holsome eyre soyle fayre grene lusty playnes goodly sene also haboundaunt vitayle replenyshed may auayle osteyng souldiours first land freshe floures plenteous corne grayne wyne fruyt yt thynge laye baraine beastes foules passyngly plentee fast adioyning see full habundaunt fyshe fynde season euery maner kynde whan yt castell grekes sea londed ferre without abode arme went vpon theim make hidous shoute stuffyng castel wt meyne strong behinde toke waye guydo fynde towarde foen knyghtly set vpon right forth grekes eke anone mette vpon fyde right surquidous inly full pryde clenly armed harneys stele freshe arayed besene wele fielde thicke sworme eche syde men may beholde seen spradde playne downe vnto ye strond tyll laste mette hande hande yoyne wt square speres groud hurtle yfere many bluddy wounde good day saluynge stroke felle men hardeen rynge bassenettes fieldes rounde cruelly fyre sprange oute amonge tuftes brode bryght shene foyle golde fethers whyte grene eke brestes perced many shelde courser fledde abrode fyelde many layde mortal stounde full deadly pale lowe vpon grounde face gruf bluddy streames wyde aldermost vpon grekes syde slaughter discomfyture mightly troyans dyd endure till laste fewe multitude grekes hewe mo forty one force abacke muste gone nothyng lacke manhode dare seyne many haue ouer layne longer may fyelde soiourne castel home agayne retourne full great haste suche myght escape away aliue rape drede death toke flyght horse backe troye towne full ryght wonder though haste faste gate chace grekes laste cruelly pursewe myght remewe troye syde forweryed fyght grekes slewe full myght might atteine may raunsom mercy gayne none estate without excepciowne vnto tenedowne grekes went sette aboute troyan none myght escape yt bulwerkes ywonne skale walle begoone made saute manfully ofte eke troyans stode lofte dryue enter ne myght caste stone quarelles bright bowe turkey shote arbalasters gonners standyng corner also caste wylde fyre yrous hate full hote desyre lyke manly men selfe deffende aye grekes vp ascende cruelly dryuen grounde tyll without ordynauce haue foude gynne deuysed none gonne great caste stone bent toures ryght lyne large sowes lowe myne vpon walle gone thycke made lyme stone entre many wayes seke sette bastyles hurdeys eke rounde aboute harde walle skalyng ladder sawtes marcyall gan vp caste hokes holde vp ascende sturdy grekes bolde tyll troyans crestes caste great stone whyle woulde laste roller eke grekes oppresse wonder manly dyd busynesse deffence made plonge low caste quarell shote bowe olyettes necessytee put may none broke neckes shulder bone fell downe square stone lyen dead pyteous pale hewe grekes aye gan saute renewe multytude troyans assayle withstande gynnen fayle feble rescuse came none force grekes gone ye walles haue broke troyans cruelly wroke fynally lefte none alyue slea kylle blyue walles baners haue sette yonge olde myght bette goth wracke vpon troye syde wyll longer byde treasour golde may fynde caste heape together bynde make spoyle within haste walles begyn pynacle toures also dungeowne brenne hewe bete downe soyle made euen playne great pray anone went againe shyppes glad lyght chere fyre flawmes clere castell consumed ybrent auyse ryght prudent manly man worthy agamenon let make anone conuocation grekes bad shulden bryng golde treasour without taryinge pray wanne tenedowne presence conclusyowne may make distribucion amonges without exception lyke desert vnto pore ryche departeth euery man lyche moste suche dyd best deserue hym selfe lyst nothyng reserue hath leuer hertes good suche spente owne bloud manfully castell wynne largesse fyrst begyn ne fayleth well spede helpe men whe hath nede loue foloweth fredome comenly phowe agamenon assembled counsayle noble grece determyned sente vlyxes dyomede ambassade kynge pryam capi xix kyng let make crye al kinges lordes ostie duke erles come euery coste next morowe afore appere nyght ypassed phebus gan clere hemysperye larke songe whan yt king amonge grekes stronge vpon playne see royall faste moste chife pryncipall lordes set degree king sawe oportunitee made scilece euery lyeges standynge enuyron kyng chere sad iocounde speche full faucounde began tale sobre countenaunce effect whiche substaunce syres quod full worthy degree verye ryght necessytee compelled hygh lowe myght lyke ye well knowe redresse thynge amys worlde reported force power myght worthynesse euery wyghtes syght renowmed worshypable ydempt iudged moste able people lyklyest stonde perfourme haue take hand euer grutcheth sayth nay yet semeth paye thylke power moste acceptable vnto goddes longest stondeth stable deuoyde surquidry pryde kouth vpon euery syde eche lande one many harmes greues haue befall rancour onely pryde wylfulnesse inportable coulde expresse pryde done offence hygh goddes maken resystence tho surquydous whiche vyce contraryous ne may place abyde good fayth manhode pryde hath acqueyntaunce outher frendshyp alyaunce proude man confederate herte hyghe lowe estate nedes must euer many necessytee lothsomest enmy contrayre nothyng may man moche appayre pryde soth highe lowe degree wherfore rede playnely wee foule vyce herte arrace quarell may haue grace specyally dedes conueyed euer fall ryghtwysenesse voluntee trouth sothfast guyde v derecte rightfull lyne shall quarell aye honour shyne contune full felycytee pand ferthermore knowen ye come done vengeaunce frendshyppe alyaunce vpon pryam wronges done olde hym haue ofte tolde hereupon haue grounde ytake maked wake manful hande castelles stronge beate downe stonde haue longe take rychesse founde slewe men many bluddy woude harmes mo done countre wote well enmytee vnto v great moche afore dare saye double yf auenged myght v echone anone ye shulde see great ire cruell huge execute without refuge yet soth wote haue espyed beynge though askyred yet dare saye vtterly well ware faste ouermore wote well also harmes haue whiche yet freshe grene stronge mighty susteyne werre v anone wolde gynne yet citie whiche walled stronge toured rounde wenen fully doute meyne haue gathred theyr allyes shall wyn smale werre stryfe soth hath prerogatyfe aduauntage countre hym selfe deffendeth namely stuffed stronge frendes hym besyde alyes doth abyde lyke rauen fether blacke within nest often tyme make agayne faukon gentyll nature full harde diffence whyles hy may endure vanquysshed outrayed yet whyle faukon delayed whyles rauen besyde nest doth flee within courte lybertee euery foule frowarde areste daunted owne neste yet wordes ne saye wyse putten fraye knyghtly hertes manly stable shulde doutable troyans fully shall confounde citie habounde playnly destroye albe stronge nowe amonge shall fynally consumpt death thorowe grekes sworde yelden vp breth pbut cause without drede saye thus ye take hede pryde presumpcion aduerte discrecion prudently reason nede haste may brydell lede ordeyne hense wende laude prayse ende may reported haue deuysed many man hath aduised pursuite lacke prouidence se tofore aduertence shuld fall deth hath brought suche wylfull hast good thought v fore examynacion well discussed reuolucion pof thynkyng ofte repente fyrst remembre pryam sent v late exyon yet holde kynge thelamon whiche v without aduisement vndiscretely denyed assent whiche hath v none aduauntage grounde rote full great damage wyse purueyaunce made tho delyueraunce harmes great eschewed parys pursewed temple faire cythera buylded besyde cirrea treasour great also iewelles thense ladde troye great rychesse slaughte men heauinesse yet made quene heleyne throughout grece great payne menelaye ben nowe vnwrought foresene thought wysely tofore restored exyon harmes ne one ensewed v sothfastnesse spent labour ydelnesse treasour good wasted vayne come ferre fetche agayne quene heleyne costes inportable withouten harmes eschewable yet ne wote whether ioye aduersytye thynge shall tourne syth ofte syth dependent doubte fatall thyng vnsyker vnstable fro gynnynge often varyable ende sene fortune transmewe gery course therfore eschewe harmes possyble lykely fall counsayle amonge al vpon arryuaile trauayle eschewe matter sewe pryamus without sende fyrste agayne restore quene heleyne ryght reason harmes done eke parys trespasse offencion iustely maken restytucion may worshyp honour retourne home without labour assente requere axynge lyste folyly wylfulnesse refusen worthynesse double assured syker grounde iuste tytle troyans confounde thynges two shalbe vnder pyght fyrst power borne vp ryght shall v fyght quarell dareyne balaunce euen weye atwixe v twayne fyne shalbe excused tofore haue wylfully refused iuste profers made afore shalbe worlde therfore without spot trespasse blame mysreporte hyndrynge name foly shall ynoted wylfull wodnesse playnly shall stande free power vse euery man shall v well excuse though execucyon takynge vengeaunce offencyon men chylde eche secte age shall death holden passage sworde without mercy pace one better grace bvt yet tofore counsayle taketh hede ye measure bede holde beste moste syckernesse worke good auisenesse amonge selfe longer tarye whiche counsayle contrary varyaunt opinyon saue discrecion assented playnly ende chosen haue pryam sende amonges ambassyat spede vlyxes wise worthy dyomede whiche anone gan ready make shope forth waye take towarde troye lyne ryght sonne shone full shene bryghte holdyng course fyry sphere mydday arke wonder bryght clere gylte eche hyll vale playne roche beames dyd approche walles gate towne go without noyse sowne full well sene porte ryght manfully waye ladde paleyes streyght lyne nedeth asyde declyne courte large wyde square thei ful knightly wight wold space vnto effecte manly procede charge without feare drede commyng tho refused tho dayes peraunter vsed haue conduite embassadrye custome man denye suppose entre passage come message courte builded royally come fyrst meruayled greatly royall syght huge strength well complete brede length ne lyfe tofore sene none fayre yet wonder paleyes together gone paued iasper stone tree amyddes stode loke thought good musyng artifyciall erecte sette magyke naturall engyne workemen curyous subtyll craftes supersticious worke nycromancye profounde castynge phylosophye apparaunce yllusyon outher crafte incantacion vp downe casten mynde reason myghten fynde rote grounde wonder worke trouthe derke wytte though longe trace pryuitee compare conceyue possyble eye vysyble soth without fable mannes hande palpable whiche stocke guydo tolde sothfastnesse pured golde whiche shone bryght somer sonne enlumyne thinges donne body maste ryght proporcyoned goodly syght substanciall huge strengthe twelue cubytes body length croppe rounde large brede compasse gan flourishe sprede playne aboute enuyrowne bowes shadowed vp downe ryche braunches leues fayre twayne twayne ioyned payre one golde another syluer shene meynt among wt stone whyte grene rede sapher hewed euery daye blomes renewed blossomes many sundry suyte stone inde bare stede fruyte sayth guido tell grekes longer dwell holde theyr waye many sondry wente parfourme fyne entent tyll atteyne chamber pryncypall pryamus see royall lyke estate full kyngly wyse sat aboute ful prudent ful wyse lordes settes hym besyde whan grekes surquedous pryde sterne cheare frowarde coutenaunce lytell remembraunce gentylnesse curtesye guydo doth playnly specifye enteryng taken haue theyr place thopposyte kynges face set theym downe without sermon obeysaunce salutacyon worshyp honour reuerence done kyng excellence preiudyce gentylnesse anone vlixes gan expresse cause theyr comyng kyng pryamus without abode saying euen thus forberyng presence kynge meruayle haue wondrynge though honour dewe comynge salewe syth ne longeth sothe thinketh rancoure hertye enmyte deadly hate salutacions fayned false affection shewe hertes ben fyre naturally man shall desyre enmye helthe welfare platly lyst spare shortly shewe fyne entent lyke hauen commaundement message agamenowne noble kyng worthy renowne whych v hath sent seyne vnto quene heleyne rauyshed grekes lande brought troy force mighty agaynst ryght vyolence wherfore shortly without offence iustly axe without demaunde thou anone rightfully commaunde menelay sent agayne axe vayne thou make restytucion wronges done regyon pylfres great slaught robberye paris done wylfull tiranye whych thy son susteyned errour wronfully maynteyned wherfore come fully condescende without grutching wronges amende thou mayst best goddes queme lyke thou mayst thy reason deme right requireth worke wyse thou despyse execute haue tolde truste right well lesson thou shalt lere whych thou thine shall hereafter rewe without feyning thou shalt fynde trewe thou better ende make cruell vengeaunce shall take fynally shuld fayne force death quarell shall darayne vpon vpon thy bloud raunsomles golde good questionles reporte merciles riche stronge cyte shall downe bete ylayde ful lowe walle toures also ouerthrowe beth well aduysed axyng despysed wysely worke haue sayde sodaynly king priamus abrayde hasty yre ne might abyde grekes whan sawe pryde great outrage presumpcyon without abode delyberacyon vlyxes anone gan breake vnto euen thus speake pi wonder greatly myn aduertence beyng astoned presence vngoodly ye dare make demaunde lyke ye power commaundt constrayne byddyng obey feare durst saye maner thinge ye axen contrayre ye requyre wherof sothly herte amened threttes inwardly agreued astoned surely lyfe ye hardy excyte vylaynously myn honour prouoke wordes worke trusteth right wele wyll passe boundes neuer dele rather shortly ende axyng ought condescende pfor consydre fyne entente syttyng conuenyent kynge graunte axing though yt stode myschefe captiuite without recure vttraunce ybrought outrage playnly thought axe hym ye axe sothly yet beleue ye accomplyshyng may much auayle ye haue sayd platly ye shall fayle purpose saye god toforne mauger might though ye sworn request euery man syght wanteth grounde trouthe righte axe satysfactyon selfe fyrst occasyon whan ye slewe father lamedowne lyeges brent eke towne many harmes soughte causeles tho ye wrought longe reherse whych daye daye herte perce syster eke called exiona regyon ye haue ladde away whych vnto worthinesse ytreated lyke gentilnesse pand ye would amendes haue wrongly whylom saue thynges peace stynt werre haue sente grece ferre onely haue exyona agayne whych sonde ye hadden disdayne cruelly vngoodly wise messenger ye gan tho despyse vnueth ne might escape awaye grece ye knowe naye vngoodly cheare good fayth lyst nowe heare request gyuen audience axyng great offence leuer shortly deyen condescende ought ye requere wyl fully conclusyon knowen agamenon haue leuer doubtles fynally werre peace syth ye haue done great trespace trouthe selfe place cruelly anone ye shulden dye offyce embassadrye agaynst death fully diffence bolde withouten reuerence presence thret speake truste right wel shuld anone wreke wherfore haste without wordes mo counsayle ye ago sight voyde cyte thus standeth while se herte may entre gladnesse fret yre holdeth distresse good fayth may sustene inportune rage tene inwardly bindeth whyle diomedes tho began smyle sayd anone thus vnto kinge thou cominge thine herte hast mykle payne v beholde twayne art therwith inly set fyre shalt thou neuer withouten yre thy life deuoyde wo syth thou hast many cruell fo grekes entred thy lande hundred thousand almost thyn hande agayne whose might yu mayst ye assure resyst playnly endure consyder well stronge thou shalt wyt peraunter longe manly men well arayed expert armes olde assayed diffence may agayne theim vayle wyte eke well thou mayst fayle death sworde theyr hande deye thyne seye though proudly thou speake thy tunge onely wreake afermest thou mayst acheue better bostyng wordes leue wyse counsayle taketh better hede bvt haste agayne diomede surquidous inly full pryde rose vp kynges syde swordes drawe wold haue fal al hewen among theim hasty yre brenning glede tyll pryamus gan taken hede rose vp seyng disease manfully rage gan appease theim diffending vpon death lyfe none theim hardy stryfe embassadoures harme greue though fole foly leue presume speake vnconningly wyse man must suffer pacyently though happe offence folishe speche lacke sapyence wyse man ne ought sothe sayne taken hede speake agayne fole pertynent shewe foly right conuenient wyse sothly suffraunce porte haue tolleraunce vnto foles belongeth kindely without aduyse speake folyly vndiscretly mening fulfyll wyse man heare styll tyll se tyme haue pacience dissimule aduertence rage foles last throwe tunge fole oft knowe leuer wel assure persone domage endure suffer messengere court haue wronge great lite swerde rancoure may alway bite vengeaunce thyng nought oft falleth wronge wrought lytel excesse foloweth great reprefe haste aye medled wyth myschefe wherfore byd ye sytte adowne wise presumpciowne attempteth maner wyse sygne worde despyse thembassadoures grekes sente let theim frely declare theyr entente ye whyles kepe lippes close sodaynly eneas rose whych next kinge helde see inwardly rancour fret ne myght selfe refrayne sayd syr ye disdayne shall saye semeth wel according one hath sayd amys rekly spoken vnaduised foly chastysed maye example take wel ware noyse crye make specially open audience offende royall excellence sothly yet wote well might gouerne playnly syght hastinesse without auisement shulde commaundement death deserue great offence trewly yet ne presence twayne haue yspoke without abode shuld anone wroke worthy ryght well sittyng whan fole presence kinge bolde hardy presumpcion take indiscrescion thinge reherse concluding sentence preiudyce magnificence taught better gouerne large tunge konne bet diserne whan shal speake whan pea suffer renne lese doth spoke hath large wherfore haste counsayle charge without abode worde mo syghte anone ago best rede anone ful proudly diomede astoned sterne loke eneas yre quoke answered agayne wordes fewe sayd syr thy wordes doth well shewe thou thou art ryght wise well king doth thyne aduyse hath nye counsayle ne maye erre degre art rightful thy iudgement wylfullnesse without aduysement cause lorde bondes pace would god place myght fauoure fortune mete leysure oportune lyke desyre canst well endite olde fable thy labour quyte thanke thy gentyll chere knightly thou hast v shewed truste well therto haue therof drede tho vlixes diomede gan interrupte wordes prudently sayde full aduysely best stynt still know fully thy quod vlyxes full manly kynge go hense without taryinge thy sight agamenon make playne relacion thy aunswere ordre horse wenten sodaynly shorte time hast way come saye kinge satte tentorye worde worde came memorye reherse substaunce euery dele wherof grekes like nothing wele conceyuing full remedye reporte embassadrye saue onely vtterly procede theim shall gouerne nede agayne troians necessitee well wote may none assented wyl dede puruey theim fast theim spede storye ye shall fynde bvt fyrst therof maken mynde must whyle eneas endyte myne auctour lyst hym wryte whych sothly bokes saye manly troian worthy eneas anchises sone great worthinesse whylom gete venus goddesse conqueroure many regyon whan troye brought destruction wente waye large see called tyrene saylyng forth goth many coste many streyght passage many daunger tyll cartage ryued thense gan sayle conquest great ytale rome hath waye take whose spring auctours mencion make came augustus cesar emperour whilom noble conquerour renowne daye doth shine enee emperour iustyne bokes called autentykes full playnly wryt therin rubrykes cesar cesares named yet ryght eneades enee name shoulden beare whych fro troye comen fere vnto ytayle eneas haue tolde cesar descended downe lyne ryght ful manly royall fyrst rome sceptre imperyall maugre theyr myght gouernaunce wysedome set ordynaunce common thynges touchyng cytee procede enee hooly lyfe knyghthod ye lyst reade ceryously ye may se ful autentyke style eneydos compyled vergyle albeit noble clerke graue afore coplete werke bokes olde maken mencion phow agamenon sent achilles thelephus ilande messa vytayles slewe king ordeyned thelephus kynge ca xx bvt nowe agayne agamenon without wyll style retourne whych kyng soiourne matter delayes make haste hath counsayle take lordes beyng present hath sent one al earles duke kinges pand sayd syres amonge thynges iourney necessarye counsayle longer tarye fyrst make ordynaunce one assent prudent purueaunce alder fyrst shape v vytayle without whych none hoost may auayle parfourme iourney thryftely wherfore reade fast lykyng plesaunce yle ful habundaunce called messa sende anone one worde assented euery chone chosen haue worthy achilles thelephus sone hercules execute purpose fynally many worthy theyr company ychosen hoost anone achilles messa gone whych lande ryche plenteous reygned kynge worthy famous tentran hyght whych tranquylyte without werre aduersyte holde sceptre royall sete yle pleasaunte mete albe saye lytell yle kyngedome longeth cecyle hath name gyuen plente messane huge great cite full plenteous se lande whych kyngdome vnderstande sayde messena mess latin habundauce fruyt corne wyne aryuayle playnes large wont stuffe charge merchaunt shyppes straunge fer countre thyther sayle large sea fetche vitayle aye yeare yeare fro many coste landes farre nere onely eschaunge merchaundise eke also bokes deuyse guido full playnly telleth v kyng called messanus countrey first messa toke name tyme great fame passyng ryche wonder plenteous dare frygyus boke maketh mencion shortly telleth conclusyon achilles thelephus also messena togither go thre thousande grekes chosen manly men amonges theyr route whych fast gan londe kynge gan vnderstonde theyr comyng descended downe worthy regiowne horse foote stele armed bryght agaynst grekes manfully fyght theim deuoyde playnly yf sodaynly thus skermyshe gan atwixe grekes mortall fone parte many one slayne hurte death ywounded neuer lykly therof sounded pfor treate theim atwene swerd sharpe speres square kene go ground euery man foo confounde labour dyd busynesse though grek theyr worthinesse theyr foen much londe ywon yet retyre begon meruayle none bycause theyr fone alwaye thre noumber agaynst one time may none till achilles gan beholde se mortall slaughter vpon grekes syde tourning ye backe wt woundes large wide hasty rancour chaungen gan bloode yre furious woode whan behelde men lese theyr lande wt swerd whiche helde hande made waye kylled bare downe felde like fierse lyowne fared sothe yt men slawe makyng foen backwarde withdrawe grekes manly recomforte maugre theim made resorte pand euer waye stode without mercy kylleth mode gayneth nought crueltee doubtles ne manhod passyng renowne worthynesse knighthod eke high prowesse grekes daye fynallye vanquished without remedye helpe recure achilles sturdy wall gan serche sheltrouns theyr rage brake tofore whose face fomen go wrake pand alderlast whan gan espye tentran kyng chyualrye defende selfe lyke worthy knyght lyon bare fyght grekes oppresse achilles cruell hardynesse ne would cease pursewynge warde tyll came king manly force stoute full pryde makyng waye rounde euery syde agayne whose might nothyng might auayle pand tentran fyrst auentayle raced hath rent male asonder al hewe wonder consydre daye cruelte al broke hath bassenet wyth many cruell wounde myght smyt kyng grounde haste maked hath let head rende bassenet merciles vengeaunce harme gan heyght auaunce fully purpose shulde dead raunsomles gan amyn heade blody swerde despytous herte castyng playnly shulde asterte ire furyous pbut fortune befell ryght thus thelephus yonge lusty knyght casuelly therof syght achilles maner ful behelde stroke anone bare vp shelde gan achilles mekely preye haue pytye deye syth laye wounded almost deathe brought poynt yelden vp ye breathe beseching beningnyte manly routhe eke knightly pyte withdrawe hande grace graunt life lytell space syth euery knyght gentilnesse enmye spare whan distresse vttraunce brought specyally whe mercy requireth humble voluntee pto achylles feruent yre rancoure set fyre aunswered agayne lyst preye nolde pryde wyll obeye gyn werre nede highe disdayne indignacion hauyng truste presumpcion manhod myght auaile agaynst grekes holden battayle preuyd playnly ende otherwyse shortly wende dyche iustely falle hath made malys v pwhere wyll entencion gaue vnto hym none occasyon vpon syde platly fer nere ministred hym matere lande menten damage hym selfe grounde rage without offence done hym v pand efte agayne yonge thelephus humbly required hath hym achylle knyghtly routhe axyng fulfyll haue mercy hym case father kynge whylom quod thelephus bonde confederate whiche lyeth nowe disconsolate expectant deadly face vpon houre whan goste shall pace gyrte ala wt many mortal woude pand bycause haue found afore tyme assured great kyndenesse manhode gentylnesse boundes regiowne vnto highe renowne whylom casually gan ryde shewed soth vpon euery syde full royal chere great humanite bounde duytee remembre haue mynde doubtles elles semeth vnkind wolde name foule twyte parte wolde acquite beseche respyte lyfe achylles withouten stryfe delyuered hath story telleth thus tentran frely vnto thelephus whether hym lyste sauen spylle hym wyll hath consydered woundes grene mortall sothly kene nede must dye gayne remedye auayle maye medecyne houre whe pheb westward gan decline battayle brought ende whyle grekes shyppes wende meane whyle tentran payne woundes gan complain without staunche pyteously blede offycers faste gan spede lytter made tho full royall toward paleys douge owne pryncipall cary hym softe easyly pand prayer full benyngly thelephus also achylles conueyed hym among prese tyll brought hym lyst receyued lyke degree full royally kyng aye languysshyng drewe towarde endynge might longer drawen forth length wofull lyfe weke strengthe spirite must algates wende haste caused sende achylles thelephus whan came sayd vnto thus psyres quod full worthy degree helth honour longe prosperitee vnto goodly aduenture whyle lyfe may dure specyally oh thelephus whiche haste gracious gentilnesse paynes stronge onely grace lyfe prolonge death ala may eschewe sworde parte remewe without recure knytte bytter bondes vpon brincke fall fatys hondes lyfe fully dispeyre whiche body neuer myght haue heire daye successyon gouerne lyttell regyon whiche lykely stande disconsolate gouernaunce fully desolate erst wan full great trauayle day werre stronge bataile haue kept ye well knowe echone defended maner fone withouten losse yeres heretoforne recurlees yore lorne ne helpe eke socour hercules great conquerour whylom father thelephus stronge mighty chyualrous whose manhode whose hardinesse knyghthode great worthynesse whiche daye day new memorye foen vyctorye daunted made ferde rygoure sharpe swerde fynally manlyhede caused reygne possede maugre might peace quyete septre crowne royall seate none tyll dead hardy lyfte vp head agaynst speake wordes fewe wherby may fully declare shewe euydence little yle perteynent longeth cecyle hercules memoryall sette pillers conquest royall ryde gon tho ferre columpna yet name beare hym called herculea though saye hyght herracula name chaungyng corrupcion whiche lande whylom mansyon people wylde barbarye whiche kyngdome magnyfye frederyke sothly secounde golde good passyngly habounde chosen emperour rome towne mighty gouernour whylom eke kyng cecyle whiche made reyse large yle myghty toure hyghe thycke wall sayth guydo memoryall put name longe remembraunce soyle pleasaunce floures freshe many sondry hewe bokes lande named newe ycalled vnderstande fayrenesse lusty newe lande tentran aye lyinge payne faste gan houre attayne cruell death afore lordes made haste thelephus call presence mortall chere sayde openly men myghten sonne quod syth nedely must pace worlde gayne may grace lyfe saue mannes myghte bycause equytye ryght compelled iustly sentence declare clerely conscyence tofore death herynge prese saye thy father hercules wyse worthy knyghtly man whylom lond conquest wan whiche onely godlyhead stocke manlyhead toke vnto comyssyon gouernaunce regyon free wyll hole regally nolde selfe countrey occupye sothly yet ryght lasse loue syth shall passe full entent laste wyll graunt ryght skylle heire iustly succede longe honour therin thy lyfe lede makyng protestacion full token confyrmacion wyll fynall myne hearte fro whiche man may diuerte vpon syde vtterly declyne pfor fyrst wyll dissent lyne together combyne one fro whiche thyng man may gone desyre laste langour thou playnly successour fynally thus conclude deme vnto septer diademe delyuered euery circumstaunce wyll assuraunce made write testament fyne concludynge laste entent full piteously besought thelephus hertely manly routhe knyghtly gentilnesse deuer busynesse death like estate royall halowe holde feast funerall solemply exequies sodeynly without wordes mo kyng tentran yeldeth vp goste went waye note coste deme suche mystyhede whan perca broken threde rocke forth waye thelephus marbell graye curiously tombe made carue dead corp therin conserue full rychely aboue graue epythaphe anone dyd graue honour playnly expresse knighthode worthynesse howe goste deuorced letter ryche golde aboue enboced rounde aboute wonder curious tombe sayden playnly thus lyeth tentran kyng doubtles whylom slayne cruell achylles scepter regallye hooly gaue whiche man may denye thelephus sonne hercules whiche tombe resteth nowe peace whan perfourmed euery thynge thelephus messa crowned kyng hyghe lowe one assent solempnely open parlement made fayth hym ydone homage lyke degree age hole herte best entent othe assured sacrament trewe lyeges receyued kyng pthan achylles without taryinge whan sette peace gouernaunce without grutchinge varyaunce shyppes anone made carye euery thyng necessarye grekes corne fruite vitayle fleshe fyshe might auayle hosteynge helpe nede downe sea dyd lede fully vessell stuffe lade thelephus made stylle boundes regyon abyde conclusion helpe diligence busynes discrete prouydence agayne myschyefe scarsytee whan nede myght socour albe lyke sayth guydo achilles full fayne wolde haue go abode sothly beste bonde assured fully beheste euery thynge grekes releue haste achilles toke leue thelephus gan anone sayle shyphes stuffed vitayle towarde grekes made menciowne shorte tyme tenedowne aryued taken hath grounde knyghtes likwise hole sounde pand agamenon fyrste hath made full relacion exployt lyke fall presence lordes sittyng enuyron many worthy knyght pand fyrste messa telleth fyght whan entred welcomyng ceryously tolde eke kynge tentran hyght playnly also achylles amydde fyelde hym slowe death hole entent fully ordeyned testament thelephus also heire tolde eke repayre vnto sea eke vyttayle pand thelephus wyll fayle sende may please whiche thynge grekes great ease brought herte lyke wonder well achilles tolde euerydell greatly preysed hygh prouydence manhode sapyence beynge bare achylles ygo lodgynge lyttle besyde knyghtes vpon hym abyde myrmydones full glade comynge hym receyued longeth kynge abode rested hym whyle pbut guydo declyneth style grekes troye towne must also make digressyowne myne auctour steppe sewe lyke conuenient dewe matter syth guyde whyle grekes sette asyde wyll reherse dare frygyus troye booke declareth vnto v ceriously maketh menciowne lordes came troye towne helpen manly defence agaynst grekes maken resystence ordynaunce many dyuers thynges came erles duke kinges dare playnly made mynde reade boke ye may yt fynde pand alder fyrst reade specyally speaketh kynges three full manly men also great fame reherseth name kyndomes yet wryteth thus pthe fyrst theim called pandarus reade tapor seconde thirde andrastrus lyke founde guydo lyst specyfye thre thousande knyghtes companye manly men euerychone pand yle called coleson lyke dare listeth expresse came also excellent prowesse pkynges foure whiche fyrst hath wrytte ynamed carras seconde hyghte ymasyus nestor thirde iiii amphymacus fyue thousande worthy knightes came manly fall vpon grekes helping towne fro ye prouince knowen great renowne called lycye came kyng glaucon brought sonne sarpedon noble knight armes full famous allyed kyng pryamus thre thousande yf shall fayne came knight wt lordes twaine pand larysse ryche lande also fynde camen kynges two quite manly ought thousand knight troye brought pand kyngdome named lycaowne euphemus kyng great renowne brought hym dare doth wytnesse thousande knyghtes great worthynesse fyue hundred dare telleth v came hupon epedus many knyghtes plate syluer bryght hym eke kyng yt remus hyght brought iii thousande troye many myle tabaria large mightye yle duke foure chiualrye erles viii came companye hauynge armes great experyence bare without difference men ye fyelde chiefe golde eueryche shielde wherby kynge holy nauy amonge knowen mighten albe bore eke also fro trace kynge pylex name fro thylke trace moste excellent whiche plage oryent haueth scyte fro mighty kyng thousande knight brought cominge myne auctor recordeth eke also hundred knightes troye go alchamus worthy duke famous came pilex guydo wryteth thus troyans helpe great nede fro pauonye sothly reade came pretemessus noble werryour lorde lande kynge gouernour duke stupex also knyghtes thousande ladde towarde troye region storye maketh mencyon prouince standeth wildernesse woodes plenteous thickenesse wherin growe full many diuers tree forest men may se buylde house fewe lande full diuersly shewe many lykenesse queynte monstruous beastes vnkouth syght merueylous stoundmele apparence illusyon false existence wonder gastfull playnly sene dyuers goddes woodes grene apperen called satyrye bycornes eke fawny incubye cause often men falle rage lande people full sauage hardy knyghtes furyous woode desyrous aye sheden bloude greatly experte specyally shete darte spere peryllous mete caste euen lyne pand yle named boetine great araye troye citee lyke fynde came duke three fyrst called amphymus samus secounde thirde forcius sayth dare listeth lye twelue hundred knightes company pand fro brotyne made remembrance riche lande hath habundaunce spyces gummes fruites corne wine holsome rote ryndes ryche fyne wonder vnkouth precious also comen kinges two full knightly men armes desyrous kynge boetes epristuis wt brought troye ferre thousande knightes arayed werre pand fro lande called pafflagonye whiche seuered companye bookes saye hystoryall vnder plage oryentall sette ferre made rehersayle fewe none lande trauayle come nere impossyble whiche lande called inuisyble bycause onely remosion yet yt ryche regyon golde syluer also stone habundaunte plentee none full treasour good hath scyte ryche floude ynamed tygre fer eufrates sayth myne auctour called dare whiche lande stele armed clene thousand knightes came phylomene worthy kyng whose shildes drede cuirboilye guydo read golde depainte fret stone ryche world trow noe liche floudes chosen deuyse whiche haue course paradyse whiche kyng gyaunt stature makynge passyng measure stronge delyuer also fynde pand fro lande yt marcheth vpon inde kyng perses came many knightly man also hande hym wan moche honour noble kyng menon eke brother called sygomon whiche lande subiectiowne duke erles knyghtes renowne thre thousande brought plate shene speres rounde whet ful square kene ethyope came noble route pand kyngdome also doute thereo dare called came kyngfull prudent full wyse manly man named theseus eke sonne hyght archylogus thousande knyghtes company theseus full nyghe allye pryamus dissent bloud kynges twayne passyng ryche good renowmed knighthode fame albe guydo reherseth name yet storye maketh mencion agresta lyttle regyon thousand knight brought vnto troy grekes pryde daunte acoye chosen pycked ye none pand land beyond amazones lyssynya kyng epystrophus wyse worthy inly vertuous passyng counsayle discreciowne full worthy renowne preued also speciall artes called lyberall lerned expert ryght notwithstandyng worthy knyght werre peace manfull ryghte sage albe ronne ferre age storye maketh rehersayle thousande knight cladde plate mayle troye towne fynde ladde hym guydo sayth hadde wonder archer syght meruaylous fourme shap maner monstruous lyke myne auctour reherse fro nauell vpwarde man lower downe lyke horse yshaped thilke parte man maked skinne blacke rough bere couered fro colde passyng foule horrible syght whose eyen twain sparkeling bright furneis reade leuene lyghtnyng falleth yt heauen dredefull loke reade fyre chere reade good archer bowe euen morowe vpon grekes wrought moche sorowe gasted many hydous loke sterne many quoke whan hym sawe ougly horryble lothsome credible many one hath wounded death caused yelden vp breath grekes syde ye shall pand wyse assembled byn yfere kynges duke erles renowne sundry landes within troye towne byn ygathred come fro ferre sayth dare helpe werre numbre maketh mynde two thirtye thousande fynde worthy knyghtes lordes estate syth worlde fourmed create ne sene trowe one citee together assembled hygh degree knightes great multitude yet dare sothly conclude boke maketh mynde came troye smaler inde nouther moste famous renowne wt priam yborne troy towne pthat fynally trewly sought syth ye houre world wrought dare affyrme vnder phebus sphere many worthy mette yfere manly men flouryng lustynesse freshe yonge lyklynesse euery poynt shape arraye well sothly naye lyst consyder vpon outher syde world men go ryde floure knighthode worthinesse chyualrye hyghe prowesse assembled without within fully assented werre begyn pwherfore ye lysters taketh good hede delyte boke reade fyrst lyttle werre began light cause many man hath loste lyfe myschyefe pyteously yet man beware therby almost nought stryfe begonne lyste loke haue hereby nought wonne deth ala hard stound many knight caught dethes wounde without recure remedye pand woman shall lye gan stryfe pytie great mischyefe aduersytie mortall slaughter euer shulde betyde better haue sette asyde suche quarelles dere ynough myte let passe yt vengeaunce byte wysedome caste afore se suche sklaunders myght eschewed venym gynneth rype though ye men horne blowe pype whan house fyred hete sparke late treate caused wherfore gynnynge remedye put euery thynge euery wyght may deme reason pand grekes lay tenedon refreshe reste peace worthy kyng hyght pallamydes thirtye shyppes grekes lande stuffed wt knight ful worthy hande beste choyse regyon aryued vp tenedon wherof grekes whan syght reioysynge ryght glad lyght hauynge regarde vnto worthynesse afore made heuynesse absence longe grutched hym stronge ne kepte mouster athene shewe clene spotte conscyence full manfully open audyence lyke knyght gan selfe excuse stoppyng tho theron lyste muse pof absence shewyng cause sykenesse sodeyne malady costrained presence withdrawe sawe sycknesse hath law helde excused fully absence pand reuerence amonge grekes wight secounde also full wyse eke habounde golde good auyse prudent euer sette entent knyghtly wisely wolde aye well achieue soeuer gan nolde leue maugre foen maner wyse tyll sawe fyne empryse opinion amonge grekes reputacion besought wolde counsayle auisely forse euery maner thyng assenteth vnto axynge benyngly great gentilnesse grekes dyd theyr busynesse procede withouten delaye enhaste euer maye gyn syege differre nought sundry way serched haue sought wyttes tenedowne may remeue towardes troye towne hauen shippes thought moste commoditee best exployt nyght pryuely toward troye towne stode fast proudely sayle shyppes sayde great peryll might fall towarde night take sea lest derkenesse ennosed bee passage knowynge waye wherof great harme fall maye thus diuers opynyon procedyng conclusyon effecte purpose ne helde styl abyden lodged fyelde lyke entryked drede ptyll daye worthy dyomede grekes seynge cowardyse euen thus counsayle gan deuyse psyres quod present lyste one assent goodly consyder aduertyng prudently shall saye tofore openly whiche knighthode haue noble name sothly semeth oughte haue gret shame whiche holde selfe mighty stronge lande soiourned haue longe nigh yeare dursten wise remoue hense cowardise haue nought elles certaynly foen graunted folyly euen lust space liberte make theim stronge oportunite v withstande playnly hande ye may well vnderstande pfor daye daye confusiowne sought way full wisely vp downe get theim helpe meane space theim enforced aboute euery place large cite barres pali walles mascued agayn skalis trusteth theron made great ordinaunce gouernaunce haue espyed seyng drede haue herte manly procede purpose hold werre aye se differre catchen hardinesse v resyste al businesse also se trust veryly afore hand manfully began knightly forth contynued iourney better fortuned sodaynly stronge mighty hande vnauysed lande without abode afore time ariued must depriued delayed fyrst victorye honour palme high glory might sothly ne slouthe complyshed playne trouthe maugre v lande ariue strog defece agayne v striue put v stronde may win aye tarye begin sothe list lye put selfe echone ieopardye sayne fage ye trouthe tarying cowarde slouthe likely tourne v great sorowe wherfore betimes next morowe counsayle ankers vp pulle matter longer dulle enarme shippes werre vprise morowe sterre let v ordayne knightly apparayle thys hauen winde sayle manly herte lusty freshe courage course holdinge right passage towarde troye landen openlye euer fall truste sykerlye without scarmishe may ariue troye descende bliue like manly men mete v berde let v aferde dreade avoyde manhod set afore cowardise ne entre bore adaunt manhode herte worde grekes gan aduerte manly counsayle diomede effect procede dede vnto poynt nothinge wyll spare wise anone declare phow grekes laded tofore troy stoutly fought ca xxi next morowe wonderly betime phebus rose longe prime whan began full merily dawe grekes hoost shipward ginnen drawe manly herte fully deuoyde drede onely comforte diomede alder first anone awake lordes wisely gan counsayle take concluded amonge theim euerichone shippes shulde ye formest gone sea shoulde theim guye ariue man theim aspye deuised certayne marke night past singing larke grekes ben shipped without tarying high lowe rathe dawning pand first tofore hudred shippes toure stuffed many worthy werrioure gan proudly sayle charge theyr baners brode bright large displayed euery side departe fomy wawes wyde sight whelmen vp grene next theim werre enarmed clene panother hondred folowed fast bare sayles passing proudly ful many worthy knight armed mayle plate bryght foloweth hooly nauye trowe companie worthy knightes lordes degree neuer afore sene vpon see eolus fortunate eke neptune made tho none debate wt winde trouble amoge ye sterne wawes attempre wether ful mery dawes tide sayled tight troye towne caught anone sighte wherof herte full glad light whan troians first shippes se proudely sayle litell stronde sawe cast thenn londe bode arme theim hastely plate mayle iackes richly irous herte done anone toke horse forth hast gone gate made tariynge ne bide prince duke kinge lorde guyde theim gouerne hast theim forth many yerne felde great multitude amonges folkes rude manly men thriftely sayne clenly armed large playne ye grekes gan theim first beholde great nomber made hertes cold none manly theim amonge yonge freshe hardy stronge high estate low degre ne astoned se hardy troias proudly descend let grekes assende well wist seme vtterly none meane tariue onely death manly fight cowardly take theim flight conduyte playnly none sharpe sworde speres case tyll sodaynly hardy fierse kinge prothesalius gouerninge formest hundred shippes ladde gan hast ire hadde win lande first would mete theim great desyre winde gan sayle driue shippes whan shope ariue vnwarely vpon londe getteys drye sonde shippes shiuered asonder dreynt broke yon er deuoured wawy see routhe pyte se greater parte tho gone wrake while busy take drye lande filth mudde ylade troians theim ful cruell slaughter made maugre might grekes constrayned wt blud wawes ystayned mortally sothly beholde amonge sonde pale dead colde grekes lye woudes freshe grene eyre withe shote arowes kene yshadowed ye phebus beames bright vpon soyle derked light newe alway troians theim assayle grekes playnly ryuayle mortall infortunate vnwelfull disconsolate vndisposed infelicitee trowe neuer erst see ne came none hoost harder londe grekes ne wolde wonde lyfe death manly aryue befelle aduenture blyue pthre hundred shyppes ye next sewe aduysedly tyme dewe entred haste faste stryke sayle ankers caste strongly enbatayled londyng lest assayled wisely fyrst sette arbalasters gonners best archer pauysers go aforne knightly land though troias hadde sworn contrary proudely lette yet fyersly vp sette grekishe shote made withdrawe many lande laye slawe maugre strode recure suche myght moste manfully endure sette afore tyll lande haue take attones suche assaute make vpon troyans tho began fyght prothesylaus ye noble worthy knighte wonder lyfely ryght passyng stronge grekes entred amonge hardy troians euery sought armes meruayles wrought thilke daye worthinesse many troyan brought distresse went felt full vnsofte whose manhod grekes alofte thilke daye knighthod grekes great aduersite vanquished fatall purueyaunce finally brought vnto vttraunce yout abacke playnly lye auayleth chiualrye worthinesse fierse courage might helpe auauntage syth vii thousande grekes ado hundred thousad troians tho meruayle might endure wise stronde recure fewe holde felde theim selfe one thinge behelde full prudently whych tho gaue theim herte sawe mighten asterte scape life woulden fle backe nothing see fore hoost great huge waye refuge dye attones fight manfully wherfore cast shope theim knightly like manly men liues rather ieoparte cowardly foen departe lese grounde drenchen see thus longe would grekes defende theim aboue might albe many killed fight streames red bloud ran sonde large flode cruelly troians theim set spere swerd ful sharpe ground whet routhe pyte thinke till almost droue theim brinke grekes mischiefe distresse great anguishe passing werinesse theim selfe defende mate full ywery shoulde haue peryshed vtterly recureles sothe euermore ne archelaus worthy prothenor shippes aryued vnto lande sodayne happe theim stande yet full great aduersyte ariue cruelte troians yet lande win grekes cruelly begin agayne foen standen defence manly force great violence tho gan encrease blody werre newe ye soyle depeynted wt dewe first grene tourned red eche side many one lay deade vpon grounde life depryued pbut duke nestor sodaynly ariued knightes fell full irous herte right melancolious speres archiers aside entred sterne full pride sworde grounde sharpe kene ran yfere met vpon grene hoked arowes alway flewe amonge shaftes shiuer brast tourne wronge tole steled well whet longe daye haue togither met slaughter newe alwaye began euery halfe many worthy man woundes large despytous pfor prothenor king archelaus swerdes stiffe among renges kerue many troian made sterue daye passingly irous theim tauenge inly desyrous neuer seasing pursewing pand releue theim alagus kinge ylonded eke king attalus troians full enuious brenning ire fiery glede vpon theim olde hatrede knightes sodeynly fall ire bitterer gall cruelly foen oppresse assent businesse maugre theim backwarde resorte amide felde reporte choyse costreyned force manhode payned withdrawe confusiowne hast downe troye towne worthy knightes freshly armed newe deuyses many sondry hewe without abode shortly conclude came downe great multitude eche armes depaynte vpon shylde comming glittereth al felde armure sonne bryght whan entred fight grekes metynge felly enuye sette vpon fret melancolye herte courage furye mortall rage accorde none mene slaught death theym go betwene thrugh stroke axe dagger spere force compelled grekes theim retourne backwarde stronde whose rescuse anone came londe king vlixes hole nauye full knightly wyth chiualrye towardes troians enhasteth anone one herte grekes gone theyr courage hooly resume gan foen felly consume vnto death domage reuenge wight may iustly theim chalenge manhode well haue theim borne acquite harmes done beforne time like fierse lyowne amonge troians ranging vp downe vlixes wente swerde honde killeth sleeth knightly gan fonde thilke daye like man founde many mortal wounde vpon troians wrought wracke bering downe fote horse backe ire stroke kene pat time worthy philomene lorde king pafflagonye whan behelde companye many troian vlixes slawe towardes anone gan drawe horse backe spere rounde sadyll bare grounde vlixes rose vp anone right taking horse lyke manly knight anone philomene hath sayne toke eft spere rode agayne mightely violence fynally gayneth diffence smote euen ye shelde flewe asonder felde plate without fayle spere head rested mayle forged stele ful shene bright perce spere head hath might trewly made haberiowne wt stroke vlixes bore downe yet efte agayne hasteth vp anone ne stroke herme felt none raught spere sharpe whet ygrounde philomene gaue wounde myght armes twayne yrous herte great payne sheld ye plate maile smote vp auentayle gorge stocke gan glyde horse fell downe asyde full peryllously pyght vpon head knightes wenyng sothly dead toke vp layde shelde bare home hast felde great daunger might wyn grekes lord twyn troians supposed sykerly philomene withouten remedye dead astoned case daye ne befall phylomene grekes stronde outrayed arruing vp londe knighthod doubtles phylomene vlyxes vnhorsed hath mortall wounde knightly wyse troians confounde wherof astoned euerychon pbut thoas agamenon grekes hooste lorde emperour aryued vnto theyr socoure knightes menelaus eke worthy thelamonious called ayax lande come leysure haue theyr horse nome grekes troians occupye sore fighting gan fast hye towardes theim making delay frushe hast may ran yfere speres bracke herte enuyous vpon horse backe myght men worthy knyghtes se stedes eche flee styffe swordes shaftes great rounde hedes square pointes kene grounde myght men se furyous tene many knightes dead vpon grene slaughter confusyowne fell thilke time theim towne grekes myghty stronge felde contynueth longe ptil prothesylay stronge mighty king daye skarmishe fighting full lyke knyght occupyed againe troians cruelte manhode onely worthinesse aduenture werynesse refreshe taken eyre abrethe making repeyre stronde aryue thought herte gan ryue cruel yre also pyte hath caught onely se men slayne endlonge stronde theim comyng vp londe dreynt sea amonge flodes depe whych thinge gan anone wepe full pyteously aspyed whose wofull eyen might tho dryed constreynt sat nygh hert till last amonge paynes smerte cruell yre gan herte enbrace sodaynly despytous face without abode thought vpon theyr death would auenged finally attones theim deye stede toke right weye towarde foen ful yrous rage line right holdeth passage swift grayhounde yt renneth lese sawe greatest ye prefe preceth amiddes felde sworde yt hande helde grounde kerue byte full mortally aboute gan smyte troians might asterte ne ryueth vnto herte woundeth sothly death made yelden vp breath also vnhorseth cruelly met daye vtterly horse made alyght rode fled sighte presence death eschewe styll one gan theim sewe chase lyke wood lyon thus playeth theim towne tyll perseus etheopye kinge came cyte sodaynly riding many knyght many lyuely man whose coming newe began freshe skarmyshe furyous wood many greke daye lost blode fell assaute troians theim make amonge theim ethiopes blake manly bare fighting troians afore fere remounted newe assured yt helpe haue ye feld recured made theim lese also much agayne tofore wonnen playne hole mightely kept theim togyther auysely gouerned theim glaue spere shelde grekes compelled felde maugre grutche necessyte stronde backwarde flee almost dispayred mate comfortles kinge pallamides theyr rescous came aryuayle lusty freshe entreth battaile knightes hole maynee taking horse tho fast see proudly thense embushed one spere swerde yground none wise gouernement doinge haue oppressed coming manly troians wonder se theim lye slayne yonder continueth til amonge prese auenture pallamides brenning aye furious hete amid felde happeth mete worthy knight called sygamon brother kyng menon neuewe also guido doth reherse manly man kinge perce grekes daye sore oppressed knighthod expressed grekes worthinesse oft sithes brought great distresse daye great encrease pbut fortune ala pallamydes tolde hath fyelde mette spere square sharpe whette whan knighthod pride rode hym smote ye side last deadly fatall wounde stede bare hym grounde playne bloud red pallamydes lefte pale dead amonges troye forth rode bare downe euer waye stode theim furyous wood maugre troians tofore playne made resorte walle agayne manly knightes alway fast awayting ful ententifely redy honde euery great emprise tho began noyle aryse wofull clamour pyteous crye theim troye vtterly agayne grekes mighten sustene mortall swerde sharpe kene noble worthy famous knyght pallamydes great myght longe daye hath yborne agayne foen knightly persone high renowne chased hath almost towne troians echone manly made theim flee noyse entred cite hydous crye mortall shoute pwherof amened hector yssueth oute furyously hast son mar knyght maly worthy yet worthiest euer hardiest phebus beames cleare amonge sterres right appeare excellyng stele armed bryght heauenly syght nigh terre worthinesse lode sterre whych whan entred felde like reade bare daye shelde fyelde pure golde thre lion storye tolde whose coloure made mencion fynde discripcion passant reporte ryght borne brest troian knyght ye ground rote high prowesse floure accompted worthinesse manly without abode amonge knightes grekes rode lyke man cominge astoned gan thringe amonges killeth downe slethe met death afore swerd grekes go wrake wardes knightly force brake maugre theyr head seuered sonder bare downe ridyng yonder casually meteth waye pprothesylaus whych longe daye sore fought agaynst theim troye slewe tho comen waye hardy knyght worthy fierse kinge whych troians euer pursewyng theim hertely great enuye whych thinge whan hector gan espye knyghthod gan taken hede towardes tho turneth stede line right hasty ire rode swerde disteyned al blode cloue head basenet might stroke na let force mayle thicke plate fynally mortall fate swerd hector thrugh nerue bone vain worthy kynge parted hath twayne vtterly gayneth none armure agayne stroke hector endure kynge full worthinesse stronge mighty great hardinesse receyued hath last fatall wounde lyeth dead parted grounde hector forth amonge grekes rideth whosoeuer stroke abydeth refute none diffence death many greke thus daye sleyth whych theim tho waye stode sharpe swerde batheth blode also ferre might se death swerde fle mortal vengeaunce vpo wrought many greke felowe sought gan enquere might lyfe coulde neuer se none knightly haue battayle playnly dempte supposayle hector noble warryour whiche knighthode bare away floure amonge euer yet borne na greke may stad aforne day gan enchace stronde euen afore face ne durste mortall stroke abyde euery syde grekes chaced wawy sea wounded mate great aduersyte rest troyan knight anone lyke mar himselfe home troye gone whose partynge grekes efte presume manly agayne hertes resume newe fomen assayle inparte wolde auayle lyfe death sette outraunce fortune lyst wold auaunce parte agayne recure fyelde enforce might spere shielde anone forthwith maken delay wynne agayne troyans maye viii tymes sythen begonne felde haue day lost wonne lyke fortune lyste cure vp downe tourne eure whele went rounde right day wan lost groud specially desmayde whe hector came hath outraide thrugh knighthod made hert ryue resorte dyd aryue thus continued mauger myght fielde troyan knyght ptyll phebus chere gan westre downe repayred towne whiche grekes wrought afore full yll pbut hardy cruell fyres achyll aryued knyghtes myrmydones men wonte calle whyche sea taken haue playne whose comynge grekes haue agayne fyelde recured put selfe prese helpe worthy achylles whiche felly troyans fall vpon hath slayne full many one thre thousande stele armed bryght hym brought redy fyght knyghtes echone full worthy renowne whiche achylles grekes champyowne haue mercilesse crueltee slayne many troyan citie feruent mortall ire enuyous hate desyre newe newe shede bloud achylles thought dyd good sworde ye troians bloud shede soyle se lye blede rowthlesse melancolye hath hote enuye without deth may quenche sworde ful depe hath made drenth throughout day troyans bloud batheth floude whiche forged ywhette knene many ryuer sothly grene ran hurtes sore knyghtes alway pursued afore hym flee harde walles troye cytee dolefully made pyteous crye whyle fynde storye pthe grekes hoost hooly aryued lyke guydo descryued men armes suche multytude knightes shortly conclude shyppes newe landed troye astoned se abashed gan wexen sodaynly gynneth fall euery halfe passyngly great prese euer one hardy achilles sworde made sydes red laye bodyes dead wounded entre gate knightly gan debate furyously fell cruell knyght chyldren slewe father syght beholde great pyte yet slaughter tho greater numbrelesse towne perpetually confusyowne lykely euer haue ouercome pif troylus ne rescuse come yenge freshe lusty inly desyrous come paris deiphobus many worthy partye socoure grekes tho ne myght endure agaynst standen deffence pryde maken resystence worthy troylus well yt time hym quytte soth greke hytte outher maymeth made hym deye wherfore deth fled weye fyerse achylles companye nyght homewarde gan hym hye towarde grekes glorye honoure receyue hym lyke conquerour whiche tyme happely mette pand troye haue gate shet made strong throughout al ye towne pand tyme kyng agamenowne yserched hath place couenable thought agreable liklyhod conuenient euery lorde pytchen tente fylde full large space moste competent lodgyng place dewe scyte sette cite eche lorde signed shulde pand gan anone ordeyne mansyons pytched tentes pauyllyons might tentoryes haue storme rayne selfe saue deuysed habytacles tiguryes smalle receptacle shroude night also shyppes hadden moche ado might well haue horse lande ordeyne shulden stande also busye carye thynges necessarye nedefully vnto syege longe eke made tye shyppes stronge porte ankers haue caste assent busyed full faste confyrme one entenciowne set syege tofore troye towne thervpon bounde assured faste abyde whyle lyfe many laste fynally without repentaunce prudently made ordynaunce best coulde longe nyght bete fyres brennen wonder light space deuyded fro fyres sette vp lyke barrier rounde lodgyng paled fyelde compase acheue fyne purpose slyly wrought kept selfe aye close pand kynge treason fall let make watche without tentes suche rested afore mynstrelles made ouermore sayth guydo longe nyght kepe tydes tofore fyres bryght meryly sowne instrumentes made reste tentes afore wery fyghte sea faynted might others eke made armure awayte wysely agayne aduenture deceite founde vpon syde pand thus kyng knightly prouyde aduyce nothyng hym escape al night fynde dyd wake ptyll morowe rowes red phebus chare gonne sprede thus eche thynge disposed ought wyll procede tellen wrought ceryously without eke within support thirde boke begyn thus endeth seconde boke thyrde boke pof first battaile wherin hector shewed hym selfe valyauncye tofore capitulo xxii wvhen aurora pale lyght vnder ye mantel mirke night curtyne hewes fade yshrouded derke shade abashed rud dy defyne femynyne ashamed durste tho seyne bycause longe bedde leyne freshe phebus owne chosen knight whiche hydde sothly syght tyll stede called flegonte enhasted hym aboue oure orizonte appollo beames clere hath recomforted oppressed chere saye dawnynge tytan vp east rysinge hete atempre ryght softe hemisphere glade lofte pthe houre troyan champiowne gouernour werres towne worthy hector whiche cite nexte pryam souereyntee towne guyde knightly excellence manhode sapyence troyan knyghtes lorde eke cheuetaine whiche hath commaunded large playne hyghe lowe exceptynge none kynges prynces lordes euerychone morowe mete yfere araye mustre appere lyke name estate besyde temple whylom consecrate goddesse called dyane moste honoured riche phane array haste lyke deuyse knyghtly man pand playne passynge fayre se sette amydde troye cite smoth right faire full freshe floures worthy noble werryours troye towne togyther assembled many beholde se famous
